Task instruction sent to agent 
# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# Kafka Log Retention Policy Configuration Audit

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that enforce log retention policy: the log.retention.ms and log.retention.bytes validation, the LogManager retention check, and the segment deletion enforcement for both time-based and size-based retention.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Apache Kafka codebase and identified all Java source files that enforce log retention policy. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Files Found:

**Core Retention Enforcement:**
- **UnifiedLog.java** - Primary retention enforcement with methods for time-based (`deleteRetentionMsBreachedSegments`) and size-based (`deleteRetentionSizeBreachedSegments`) segment deletion

**Configuration & Validation:**
- **LogConfig.java** - Validates log.retention.ms/bytes and local.retention.ms/bytes configurations
- **ServerLogConfigs.java** - Defines retention configuration constants and defaults
- **TopicConfig.java** - Topic-level configuration keys for retention policies
- **RemoteLogManagerConfig.java** - Remote storage retention configuration

**Orchestration & Scheduling:**
- **LogManager.scala** - Schedules periodic cleanup via `cleanupLogs()` method with configurable interval (log.retention.check.interval.ms)
- **DynamicBrokerConfig.scala** - Validates retention configuration changes at runtime

**Remote Storage Retention:**
- **RemoteLogManager.java** - Handles retention for tiered storage with `RemoteLogRetentionHandler` inner class

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details of all relevant files, symbols, and a comprehensive narrative explaining the retention policy enforcement mechanism in Apache Kafka.

It compares the current timestamp against segment timestamps and removes segments that exceed the retentionMs threshold, using the segment's largestTimestamp() or last modified time.\\n\\nFor size-based retention enforcement, the deleteRetentionSizeBreachedSegments() method enforces the log.retention.bytes policy by calculating the total log size and removing segments when the log exceeds the configured retention size limit. The cleanupExpiredRemoteLogSegments() method handles the deletion of remote segments that breach retention policies.\\n\\nDynamic configuration validation is handled in DynamicBrokerConfig.scala (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/DynamicBrokerConfig.scala) through validateLogLocalRetentionMs() and validateLogLocalRetentionBytes() methods, which validate remote log manager configuration changes at runtime.\\n\\nThe topic-level configuration keys are defined in TopicConfig.java (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/TopicConfig.java), including RETENTION_MS_CONFIG, RETENTION_BYTES_CONFIG, LOCAL_LOG_RETENTION_MS_CONFIG, and LOCAL_LOG_RETENTION_BYTES_CONFIG.
